<div id="review_1255669684" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1255669684" />
    <a title="Kathe L" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25921490-kathe-l"><img alt="Kathe L" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421550107p2/25921490.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1255669684?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathe L" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathe L" href="/user/show/25921490-kathe-l">Kathe L</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25921490-kathe-l?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25921490-kathe-l?shelf=romance-or-ya-book">romance-or-ya-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25921490-kathe-l?shelf=didn-t-expect-to-be-so-good">didn-t-expect-to-be-so-good</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25921490-kathe-l?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25921490-kathe-l?shelf=bad-boy-i-love-you">bad-boy-i-love-you</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25921490-kathe-l?shelf=3-5-stars">3-5-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1255669684" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9461064386141364787"><b>3,5 - 4 'Why the war paint, Pix?' stars!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1396621968ra/9161352.gif' width='350' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>It's funny how I always go into books expecting one thing and end up being completely surprised by it. <b>The romance in this book isn't the best thing about it.</b> No. It is the fact that it deals with something that is so serious, but that isn't showed enough. It was my first book about it: <b>eating disorders/anorexia</b><br/><br/>It's weird how a comment can change you so much. How someone calling you fat can make you starve, and make you look down on yourself. It's difficul</span>
  <span id="freeText9461064386141364787" style="display:none"><b>3,5 - 4 'Why the war paint, Pix?' stars!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1396621968ra/9161352.gif" width="350" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It's funny how I always go into books expecting one thing and end up being completely surprised by it. <b>The romance in this book isn't the best thing about it.</b> No. It is the fact that it deals with something that is so serious, but that isn't showed enough. It was my first book about it: <b>eating disorders/anorexia</b><br><br>It's weird how a comment can change you so much. How someone calling you fat can make you starve, and make you look down on yourself. It's difficult to have a high self-esteem. And Lexi here, she has an eating disorder and there's a voice inside her head <i>(we all have, the 'devil' side of our consciousness)</i> that "makes" her starve in order for her to reach <i>perfection.</i> Perfection is to be really thin, overweight, healthy? I have been overweight, healthy and really thin: the difference is in the fact that we should be comfortable no matter what size our body is. I lost weight because it could influence on my health, and I gained weight when I was more thin that I should have because I didn't want to let go of food only to fit in. <b>But it's hard.</b> It's hard to let go of the idea that I will look like a supermodel, or that perfection = thin. It's hard to let go of the 'devil' on our minds that always comes to life when someone insults us or looks down on us. <b>And this book is a hard one because of all the things I said above. It portraits them all, in a meaningful and painful way.</b><br><br><i>What else I loved about this?</i> While yes, there is a romance (a very adorable and strong one, in fact), this book also shows how far we can go for our family. Our main character, Austin, has to face and make decisions based 99% on his mother and brothers. They are not rich, so it showed perfectly the difference between Austin's life's and Rome's. Rome's wasn't perfect either, yes, but I thought Austin was way braver, smarter and caring. He was my absolutely favorite, because while I pained for Lexi, he was the thing I hoped would save her. He was kind of my hope. <br><br><i>What would you do if your friend/lover hid anorexia from you?</i> Here's the case in this book. Lexi doesn't tell anyone about her problem, even her closest friends. She hid it so well, with fake smiles, over sized clothes, skipping lunches. <s>Only Austin figured it our later.</s> I felt sick because what if one person next to you has all this secrets? A problem? A disorder? I don't have many info on this subject other then what I've read from this book, but it's not just 'go eat and sort it out'. It has a background, a development, overcoming the fear of not belonging. <b>And knowing that the author portrayed herself as Lexi,</b> it only made this book much special. Anorexia is not a fantasy, because we saw the author's struggle alongside Lexi. And Tillie Cole definitely has the gift of delivering emotional stories. <br><br><i>The romance?</i> Until 2,5/4 of this book, the romance was probably the 3rd thing I liked more about it. But man, it's in the hardest times we see true love. I've already loved Austin since the beginning, he wasn't scared to feel and cry. He wasn't a man whore. And he and his Prix (Lexi) were like a connection made in the books heaven. A thing that isn't faked or forced into a story that doesn't necessarily need it to be complete. The author deliverers romance but she doesn't forget that this book isn't about it. <br><br><b>"Why the war paint, Pix?"<br>My slow heart rate sped to a frightening rhythm, and closing my eyes, I pushed down the voice that had been in control of me for months and finally confessed, "Because I'm anorexic. I'm severely anorexic, and I try to hide it from the world."</b><br><br>This book is one of these books that you feel numb, pained, shocked. It's like I could only breathe again when I reached the last page of the epilogue. I had a hard time trying to decide how many stars I would give this, because the romance is what makes this book "lighter". And at the beginning, I had a hard time trying to understand. Like, "why are she listening to this?" or "why wouldn't she fight?" but it becomes clearer the more you read. It opened my mind to a thing I have never read about before, and for that I would never regret reading this. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9461064386141364787" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }

      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5168231439462569127">Amazon & USA Today Best Selling Author, Tillie Cole, is a Northern girl through and through. She originates from a place called Teesside on that little but awesomely sunny (okay I exaggerate) Isle called Great Britain. She was brought up surrounded by her English rose mother -- a farmer's daughter, her crazy Scottish father, a savagely sarcastic sister and a multitude of rescue animals and horses.</span>
  <span id="freeText5168231439462569127" style="display:none">Amazon &amp; USA Today Best Selling Author, Tillie Cole, is a Northern girl through and through. She originates from a place called Teesside on that little but awesomely sunny (okay I exaggerate) Isle called Great Britain. She was brought up surrounded by her English rose mother -- a farmer's daughter, her crazy Scottish father, a savagely sarcastic sister and a multitude of rescue animals and horses. <br />Being a scary blend of Scottish and English, Tillie embraces both cultures; her English heritage through her love of HP sauce and freshly made Yorkshire Puddings, and her Scottish which is mostly demonstrated by her frighteningly foul-mouthed episodes of pure rage and her much loved dirty jokes.<br /><br />Having been born and raised as a Teesside Smoggie, Tillie, at age nineteen, moved forty miles north to the 'Toon', Newcastle-Upon-Tyne, where she attended Newcastle University and graduated with a Bachelor of Arts honours degree in Religious Studies. She returned two years later to complete a Post-Graduate Certificate in Teaching High School Social Studies. Tillie, regards Newcastle to be a home from home and enjoyed the Newcastle Geordie way of life for seven 'proper mint' and 'lush' years.<br /><br />One summers day, after finishing reading her thousandth book on her much loved and treasured Kindle, Tillie turned to her husband and declared, "D'you know, I have a great idea for a story. I could write a book." Several months later, after repeating the same tired line at the close of another completed story, she was scolded by her husband to shut up talking about writing a novel and "just bloody do it!" For the first time in eleven years, Tillie actually took his advice (he is still trying to get over the shock) and immediately set off on a crazy journey, delving deep into her fertile imagination. <br /><br />Tillie, ever since, has written from the heart. She combines her passion for anything camp and glittery with her love of humour and dark brooding men (most often muscled and tattooed – they’re her weakness!). She also has a serious side (believe it or not!) and loves to immerse herself in the complex study of World Religions, History and Cultural Studies and creates fantasy stories that enable her to thread serious issues and topics into her writing -- yep, there's more to this girl than profanity and sparkles!<br /><br />After six years of teaching high school Social Studies and following her Professional Rugby Player husband around Europe, they have finally given up their nomadic way of life and settled in Calgary, Alberta where Tillie spends most of her days (and many a late night) lost in a writing euphoria or pursuing a dazzling career as a barrel-racing, tasselled-chap wearing, Stetson-sporting cowgirl... Ye-haw!<br /></span>
